	This looks like a Caesar cipher!  A shift of 13 (ROT13) cracks it:

**"A woman admires A star"** 

Here's how it works: Each letter in the coded message is shifted 13 places down the alphabet.  For example, 'N' becomes 'A', 'y' becomes 'w', and so on.  Since the English alphabet has 26 letters, shifting 13 is a reciprocal cipher - applying it *again* decrypts the message (or decrypts back to the original).

**How ROT13 works:**  Each letter is replaced by the letter 13 positions further down the alphabet. 'A' becomes 'N', 'B' becomes 'O', 'C' becomes 'P', and so on. Because the alphabet has 26 letters, applying ROT13 *again* deciphers it back to the original text!

**How ROT13 works** 
It rotates each english letter 13 places so for instance

A is paired with N to get an easily identifiable alphabet for shifting.	This looks like a Caesar cipher! The most common guess for these is a shift of 13 (ROT13). Let's try that:

Applying ROT13 to "N ymnsp ymjwjktwj N fr" gives us:

**A happy holiday A is**

Here's how the ROT13 cipher works: Each letter is replaced by the letter 13 positions after it in the alphabet, wrapping around at the end. (A becomes N, B becomes O, etc.)

**How ROT13 Works:**

ROT13 replaces each letter with the letter 13 positions after it in the alphabet, wrapping around to the beginning if necessary.  So A becomes N, B becomes O, and so on. Because there are 26 letters in the alphabet, applying ROT13 *again* decrypts the message.
